Difference between capstan and turret lathe
mechstuff4u
mechstuff4u

Jul 19, 2019Â·2 min read


Capstan and Turret lathes are the advancements of the Engine lathes and centre lathes in which the tailstock is replaced by a hexagonal turret tool head with 6 different tools in the turret where the turret tool is rotated according to process requirements in each operation. The capstan and turret lathe although appear to be identical in the first sight but a lot of differences in construction, operation, and use. In this article, you can check it out some difference between these two lathe machines.
Capstan lathe :
Lightweight machine.
These are usually horizontal lathe.
Turret head is mounted on a slide called ram which is mounted on the saddle.
Suitable for bar work.
The saddle is locked at a particular point and the ram is moved to provide feed to the tool.
Only a limited amount of feed and depth of cut are provided for machining.
The cross slide is mounted on a carriage which rests on bed ways between the headstock and the ram.
The turret tool head is indexed automatically.
Feed stop screws are used to control the distance of tool movement which is at the rear side of the turret.
No such facility to moving turret at right angles.
Feed rod gives for longitudinal feed.
Used for mass production of small size equal part.
It has hand-operated collet chucks.
Heavy cuts on workpiece canâ€™t be given because of non-rigid construction.
Turret lathe :
Heavyweight machine.
Turret tool head is directly fitted on the saddle and both of them appear like one unit.
Suitable for heavier chucking work.
The saddle is moved to provide feed to the tool.
They are heavy and durable.
More feed and depth of cut are provided for machining.
Some turret type lathes are equipped with side hung type carriage.
To index the turret tool head, a clamping lever is released and the turret is rotated manually.
Limit dogs are used to control the distance of tool movement.
Some turret lathes have the facility of moving the turret at right angles to the lathe axis.
Feed rod does not give for longitudinal feed.
Used for mass production of large size equal part.
It is accommodated with power chucks.
Heavy cuts on a workpiece can be given because of the rigid construction of a machine.
These are available in the horizontal and vertical lathe.

13/04/21, 11:28 - +91 70742 49585: A single cylinder, four-stroke I.C. engine rotating at 900 rpm has a crank length of 50 mm and a connecting rod length of 200 mm. if the effective reciprocating mass of the engine is 1.2 kg, what is the approximate magnitude of the maximum â€˜shaking forceâ€™ created by the engine?
a)533 N
b)666 N
c)133 N
d)None of the above
Correct answer is option 'B'. Can you explain this answer?
	
SHUBHAM SHEKHAR
Aug 04
Maximum Secondary force Maximum shaking force 
= mw2r {cosq + (cos 2q / n)}
[n = (l/r) = (200/50) = 4]
= 1.2 {(2p x 900) / 60}2 x 50 x 10-3 (1+(1/4))
(at q = 0Â°)
f = 666 N.

19/06/21, 18:10 - Sailesh: Internship/training application steps:
1. First, the student has to fill up the application (.doc/.docx format) and put his/her scanned signature
2. Then he/she has to forward the application to his/her departmental faculty coordinator or HOD
3. Then the departmental faculty coordinator/ HOD has to forward the application (.docx/.doc format) to training@jgec.ac.in
(The departmental faculty coordinator/hod can put his/her scanned signature in the application or simply forward it to training@jgec.ac.in stating his consent)
4. Then finally the application will be forwarded to any organization from training@jgec.ac.in with scanned signature of training placement coordinator, JGEC and of HOD, Training and Placement Cell,JGEC

Without departmental consent no students will be entertained. 
Students can't be allowed to physical training or internship within semester. Only online training is allowed within semester. They can apply training or internship physically and virtually after exam schedule as mentioned in JGEC academic calendar.
Still if any student wants to apply for training or internship without following the academic calendar, he needs HOD's permission regarding this.

20/06/21, 23:02 - +91 86373 95288: I talked to MAKAUT contact person on MAR. I had some queries. 
After discussion, the following are confirmed : 

1) *Last  year's special activity lists for 'Lock down Period" (available in MAKAUT website) is valid for this year also*. The list is valid for students of all years from 1st to 4th.

 However, a student can obtain maximum 25 points from that  "Special Activity Lists for Lockdown" out of 100 Points under MAR.

2) *For MOOC courses, as stipulated in MAKAUT website, Credits(for BTech Honours) will be awarded based on Course duration in number of  Weeks*
. For NPTEL/ SWAYAM platform Credit Points are specified. For other Platforms like Coursera, Edx, Udemy etc Credit Points are awarded based on nos of Weeks of the course, as stipulated by MAKAUt (available in MAKAUT website). Also given here.

*For MAR, any MOOCs Course may be choosen from the above mentioned Platforms and Points for MAR are awarded based on  given criteria as prescribed in Record-Sheet of MAR (available in MAKAUT website)*
.
It is observed that NPTEL is not arranging exams in regular way during this pandemic period, which posses problems to students. MAKAUT has  nothing to do in this respect.

*In certain Coursera, Edx, Udemy and Simplilearn  organized courses no. of weeks are not mentioned.*

 Again, in certain cases no. of weeks for the Courses are mentioned, but in Certificate there is no mention of Course duration (no. of weeks) or, Credit points.

*In such cases, where no. of weeks are mentioned in Course listing (but not shown in certificates), a print of that Course Listing page mentioning no. of weeks for the Course should be attached with the Certificate and accordingly Credits( for Honours)  will be awarded.*

*However, if Course duration(no. of weeks of the Course) is not mentioned either in Course list or in Course Certificate, no Credit will be awarded in those cases for BTech Honours purpose., even if  no. of hours for the Courses may be mentioned.*

 *However, for MAR, Points are awarded and not Credits.*
*It may be noted that :*
*In MAR, MOOCs Course Points are awarded based on both no of weeks of the Course/no. of hours of Course ,as specified in MAR Record Sheet. So we have to follow Record Sheet for MAR*

3) MAKAUT has stipulated other rules, norms, MAR Point Record-Sheet, lists for 1st year Honours Courses etc. All are sent to all faculty members from time to time and are also available in MAKAUT websites.

4) Certain Govt recognized Universities, Colleges or Organizations  are now arranging online Quizes, Essay competitions etc.

  Participation Certificate (award winning not necessary) of such cases will earn MAR Points.

5) Similarly, Participation Certificate(given by MAKAUT) of any Program organized by MAKAUT will earn MAR Points. 
 Program arranged on 'Environment Day' on last 5th June by MAKAUT is an example.

*All MAR Committee Members and HODs are requested, as advised by Principal sir, to forward these clarifications to all CRs and do the needful.

Regards,
Dr. Soupayan Mitra
Chairman,
MAR and Societal Outreach Committee, JGEC

26/06/21, 16:35 - Debsrijan: Dear CRSs of ME Department,

This is to inform you that the question pattern for the forthcoming even semester examination will be
as follows:

Question papers will be of MCQ type ( with the duration of 90 minutes) for B.Tech & M.Tech students.

The type of questions & marks will be as follows:

a) For B.Tech students:

i. 02 marks each for 20 questions i.e 2x20 =40 marks & 01 marks each for 30 questions i.e lx30 =30
marks.
Therefore total marks = 70.

b) For M.Tech students:

02 marks for 35 questions or same as B.Tech. guidelines.

Please share this information with all the students of your Class.

Best Wishes,

S. Bhattacharya
